Division of Upper and Lower Floors: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partition ratio

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on dividing upper and lower floors and apply the value-based method to a given scenario.

Core Idea
The lower floor's extra facilities make it worth double the upper floor per cubit according to Abu Hanifa; but value-based division is more equitable.

Partitioning jointly owned property requires fairness. When one floor has a well and stable and the other does not, how do you measure equality? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents three Hanafi views and a practical example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that the issue is the ratio for dividing upper and lower floors in a partition. Three imams within the Hanafi school differ.
The dispute is about the method of measurement, not the permissibility of partition itself.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that one cubit of lower floor equals two cubits of upper floor because the lower floor has additional benefits (well, stable, cellar).
This is based on the greater utility of the lower floor.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf argues that both floors are equal in benefit, so one cubit of lower floor equals one cubit of upper floor (cubit for cubit).
He considers the primary function of both floors as residence.
4
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's position
Muhammad proposes division based on market value: if values are equal, cubit for cubit; if one is more valuable, adjust proportionally until equal in value.
This is the most flexible and often preferred method.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is the physical ratio of division. For example, a 100 sqm lower floor with extra facilities would be treated as 200 sqm by Abu Hanifa, 100 sqm by Abu Yusuf, and adjusted by value by Muhammad.
The choice affects the size of each owner's share.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القسمة
الأصل في المذروع والكلام فيه والعبرة للتسوية في أصل السكنى كما في المرافق. قال في العناية : وصورتها علو مشترك بين رجلين وسفله لآخر وسفل مشترك بينهما وعلو لآخر وبيت كامل مشترك بينهما والكل في دار واحدة أو في دارين قيدنا بهذا لئلا يقال قسمة مع السفل قسمة واحدة إذا كانت البيوت متفرقة لا يصح عند الإمام؛ لمحمد أن السفل العلو يصلح . منفعة وتفسير لما لا يصلح له العلو كالبئر والاصطبل والسرداب وغيره فصار كالجنسين فلا يمكنه التعديل إلا بالقسمة وكيفية القسمة على قول الإمام ذراع سفل بذراعين من العلو. وقال أبو يوسف : ذراع بذراع قيل أجاب كل منهما على عادة أهل عصره، وقيل هو اختلاف حجة بينهم . قال الإمام : لصاحب السفل منافع كثيرة ولصاحب العلو منفعة واحدة وهي السكني. وأبو يوسف قال : هما سواء في الانتفاع وتفسير المسألة على قول الإمام أن يجعل بمقابلة مائة ذراع من العلو المجرد ثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث ذراع من البيت الكامل فثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث لمن العلو الكامل بمقابلة مثله من العلو المجرد وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث من السفل الكامل في مقابلة ست وستين وثلاثين من العلو المجرد فذلك تمام مائة ويجعل بمقابلة مائة ذراع من السفل المجرد ستة وستين وثلثا ذراع من البيت الكامل لأن علوه مثل نصف سفله فستة وستون وثلثان من سفل الكامل في مقابلة مثله من السفل المجرد وستة وستون وثلثان من العلو الكامل في مقابلة ثلاثة وثلاثين وثلث ذراع من السفل المجرد فذلك تمام مائة . قول الإمام أبي يوسف أن يجعل بمقابلة شيء من السفل المجرد أو من العلو المجرد قدر نصفه من البيت الكامل. ويقابل نصف العلو بنصف السفل لاستواء العلو والسفل عنده ويجعل بمقابلة شيء من السفل المجرد قدره من العلو المجرد. وقال محمد: يقسم على قيمة السفل والعلو، فإن كان قيمتها على السواء يحسب ذراع بذراع وإن كان قسمة أحدهما أعلى من الآخر يحسب الذي قيمته أعلى على النصف ذراع بذراعين من الآخر حتى يستويا في القيمة . وفي الذخيرة فإن قيل : كيف يقسم العلو من السفل قسمة واحدة عند الإمام ومن مذهبه أن البيوت المتفرقة لا تقسم قسمة واحدة إن لم تكن في دار واحدة؟ قلنا : موضوع المسألة أنهما في دار واحدة والبنيان في دار واحدة وإنما يقسم عند الإمام رضي الله تعالى عنه وإن كان في دارين بطريق التراضي فلهذا قيد في النهاية بما سبق وعلم من قوله «قوم كل على حدة» أن البناء لا يقسم بالذراع قال : وإن قسما داراً فإنه يقسم العرصة بالذراع ويقسم البناء بالقيمة . ثم هذا على ثلاثة أوجه : فتارة يقسما الأرض نصفين ويشترطا أن من وقع البناء في نصيبه يعطي لصاحبه نصف قيمة البناء وقيمة البناء معلومة أو اقتسموا ذلك وقيمة البناء غير معلومة بأن اقتسموا الأرض ولم يقتسموا البناء، فإن اقتسموا الأرض وشرطا في البناء كما تقدم فيكون بيعاً مشروطاً في القسمة، وهذا البيع من ضرورات القسمة فيكون له حكم القسمة فيجوز وإن لم تعرف قسمة البناء واقتسموا كذلك جاز استحساناً ويفسد قياساً لجهالة كانا
Book of Partition. The principle regarding the measurement and the discussion therein, and the consideration is for equality in the original residence as in the facilities. Al-Inayah said: Its example is an upper floor shared between two men and its lower floor belonging to another, and a lower floor shared between them and an upper floor belonging to another, and a complete house shared between them, all in one house or in two houses. We restricted it with this so that it is not said that partition with the lower floor is a single partition when the houses are scattered, which is invalid according to the Imam; because for Muhammad the lower floor and upper floor are suitable for benefit and explanation of what the upper floor is not suitable for, like the well, stable, cellar, and others, so they become like two different types, so adjustment is not possible except by partition. The manner of partition according to the Imam: one cubit of lower floor is equivalent to two cubits of upper floor. Abu Yusuf said: cubit for cubit. It is said each answered according to the custom of his time, and it is said it is a difference of proof among them. The Imam said: The owner of the lower floor has many benefits, and the owner of the upper floor has one benefit which is residence. Abu Yusuf said: They are equal in benefit. The explanation of the issue according to the Imam: in exchange for one hundred cubits of bare upper floor, thirty-three and one-third cubits of the complete house are placed; so thirty-three and one-third belongs to the complete upper floor in exchange for the like from the bare upper floor, and thirty-three and one-third from the complete lower floor in exchange for sixty-six and two-thirds from the bare upper floor, so that completes one hundred. And in exchange for one hundred cubits of bare lower floor, sixty-six and two-thirds cubits of the complete house are placed, because its upper floor is like half of its lower floor; so sixty-six and two-thirds of the complete lower floor are in exchange for the like from the bare lower floor, and sixty-six and two-thirds of the complete upper floor are in exchange for thirty-three and one-third cubits of bare lower floor, so that completes one hundred. The statement of Imam Abu Yusuf: in exchange for something from the bare lower floor or from the bare upper floor, half of it from the complete house is placed. He equals half of the upper floor with half of the lower floor because of the equality of upper and lower floors in his view, and he places in exchange for something from the bare lower floor the like from the bare upper floor. Muhammad said: It is divided according to the value of the lower and upper floors; if their values are equal, it is calculated cubit for cubit; and if one of them is higher in value, the one with higher value is calculated at half, one cubit for two cubits of the other, until they become equal in value. In al-Dhakhira: It is said: How can the upper floor be divided from the lower floor in a single division according to the Imam, while his doctrine is that scattered houses are not divided in a single division if they are not in one house? We answer: The subject of the issue is that they are in one house and the building is in one house; and the Imam divides even if they are in two houses by mutual consent. For this reason, it was restricted in al-Nihayah by what preceded. And it is known from his statement: 'Evaluate each separately' that the building is not divided by cubit. He said: If they divided a house, the open ground is divided by cubit and the building is divided by value. Then this is in three ways: sometimes they divide the land into two halves and stipulate that whoever gets the building in his share gives to his partner half the value of the building, and the value of the building is known; or they divide that and the value of the building is unknown, by dividing the land and not dividing the building. If they divide the land and stipulate regarding the building as mentioned, it becomes a sale conditional on division, and this sale is a necessity of division, so it has the ruling of division and is permissible even if the division of the building is not known. And if they divide similarly, it is permissible by istihsan and invalid by qiyas due to uncertainty. Was.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with the rules of partitioning (qismah) property that includes both upper floors (uluww) and lower floors (sufl). The author begins by stating that the baseline for equality in division is the original residence and facilities. He then provides a scenario from al-Inayah: two men share an upper floor and another owns the lower floor, or vice versa, or they share a complete house. The key point is that the partition must be done fairly. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that one cubit of lower floor is equivalent to two cubits of upper floor, because the lower floor has more benefits (e.g., well, stable, cellar) while the upper floor only provides residence. Abu Yusuf considers them equal in benefit, so cubit for cubit. Muhammad al-Shaybani uses value: if the values are equal, cubit for cubit; if one is higher, adjust proportionally. The text then discusses a scenario where land and building are divided separately. According to Abu Hanifa, if the land is divided but the building remains shared, the one who gets the building in his share must pay the other half the value. This is considered a sale necessitated by division, so it is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) even though analogy (qiyas) would invalidate it due to uncertainty. The passage concludes with a discussion of dividing land without dividing the building, where the resulting forced sale is allowed to avoid hardship.

Key Terms
القسمة (al-qismah): Partition or division of jointly owned property among co-owners.
العلو (al-uluww): The upper floor of a building, typically used for residence only.
السفل (al-sufl): The lower floor of a building, which may include additional facilities like well, stable, cellar.
ذراع (dhira'): A unit of length (cubit) used in measuring land and buildings for partition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, one cubit of lower floor is equivalent to how much of the upper floor?
A) One cubit
B) Two cubits
C) Half a cubit
D) Based on value

Key Takeaway
When dividing shared floors, the Hanafi school considers utility and value, not just physical area, with three distinct methods.

Claims of Error After Division Require Proof
Ruling with proof on post-division error claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a claim of error after a completed division is not admitted without evidence, and distinguish between claims that require mutual oath and those that do not.

Core Idea
A completed division is a binding contract; a claim of error is a claim to rescind, requiring proof.

This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the procedural rules governing disputes after a division of jointly owned property. The matn establishes that once division and possession are complete, a partner's claim that an error occurred is not accepted without clear evidence. The text then explores nuances: when the claim implies usurpation, when an admission exists, and the difference between fungible and non-fungible goods. We will unpack the key principles and their applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios in the matn
Read the matn carefully. There are two main scenarios: (1) one partner claims some of his share is in his partner's hand and the latter admits receipt; (2) a partner says 'I received and took some of it' (implying an extra was taken).
The ruling for both is similar: the claimant is not believed without evidence.
2
Understand the legal reason (ta'lil)
The text states: because division is a binding contract (عقد لازم), and the claimant of error is effectively seeking rescission, which requires proof. This analogy to other binding contracts is the core proof.
The legal reason is explicit: 'القسامة من العقود اللازمة'.
3
Examine the objection and response
An objection arises: if the rule is based on the need for proof, why isn't the beneficiary of an admission sworn when the admitter claims lying? The answer distinguishes the cases: here the beneficiary does not admit the lie, so the admission stands and no oath is needed.
This shows the precision of Hanafi reasoning in weighing admissions.
4
Distinguish claims requiring mutual oath (tahaluf) from those that do not
The text clarifies: if each admits receipt and then one claims the other took extra, the defendant's word with oath is taken (no mutual oath). If the claim is based on error that implies usurpation, the rules differ. For fungibles, proven error redistributes the remainder; for non-fungibles, the division is redone.
This distinction affects the procedure: mutual oath occurs only when both parties' claims are equally plausible without admissions.
5
Apply the rule to a practical scenario
Consider two partners who divide 100 sheep. After possession, partner A claims partner B took 5 extra by mistake. B denies. According to the Hanafi rule, B's word with oath is taken because the division is complete. If A brings evidence, it is considered; otherwise, the division stands.
This demonstrates the finality of division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولو ادعى أحدهم عن الضمان بالاستيفاء لا يصدق إلا ببينة وإن قال استوفيت وأخذت بعضه كان القول قول الخصم أن من نصيبه شيئاً في يد صاحبه وقد أقر بالاستيفاء لا يصدق إلا ببينة) لأن القسمة من العقود اللازمة والمدعي للغلط يدعي حق الفسخ لنفسه بعد تمامها فلا يقبل إلا بحجة، وإن لم يقم ببينة استحلف الشركاء لأنهم لو أقروا بذلك فإذا أنكر وأحلفوا عليه. ولقائل أن هذا الدليل لوجب تحليف المقر له إذا ادعى المقر أنه كذب في إقراره مع أنه لا يحلف عند الإمام ومحمد الجواب أن يقال : إن هذا إذا أقر المقر له أن المقر كذب في إقراره فلو لم يقر المقر له أنه كذب في إقراره لزمه ذلك ولا يظهر فيه أنه لو أنكر استحلف كما لو قالوا فيما نحن فيه لا أنه إذا أنكر كان مصدقاً . في إقراره فافترقا، حلف لم يكن عليه سبيل، ومن نكل عن اليمين جمع نصيبه مع نصيب الآخر المدعي فيقسم على قدر حقوقهما فيه. قالوا: وينبغي أن لا يقبل دعواه أصلاً لأنه متناقض وإليه أشار من بعد حيث شرط التحالف إن لم يشهد على نفسه بالاستيفاء، ويشير بذلك إلى أنه لو شهد على نفسه بذلك لا يتحالفان لأن دعواه لم تصح للتناقض، فإذا منع التحالف لعدم صحة الدعوى للتناقض فكذا هنا. قال صدر الشريعة في شرح الوقاية بعد نقل ما نقل صاحب الهداية : وينبغي إلى آخره. وفي المبسوط وقاضيخان ما يؤيد هذا ا هـ . قال : وأما ما لا يوجب التحالف ويكون القول قول المدعى عليه مع يمينه وهو ما إذا أقر كل واحد منهما بالاستيفاء ثم ادعى أحدهما على الآخر أنه غصب شيئاً من نصيبه إلى آخر ما ذكرناه أولاً قال : وهكذا المكيل والموزون والمذروعات إلا أن يكون في المكيل والموزون متى ثبت الغلط بالبينة لا تعاد القسمة بل يقسم الباقي على قدر حقهم لأنه لا ضرر في قسمة في الأشياء المتفاوتة تعاد للقسمة ولا يقسم الباقي وفي التجريد والأصل: الغلط في مقدار الواجب بالقسمة وهو نوعان: نوع يوجب أحدهما غلظاً يدعي في القسمة على وجه لا يكون مدعياً للغصب بدعوى الغلط كمائة شاة بين رجلين اقتسماها ثم قال أحدهما لصاحبه صابك خمس وخمسون غلظ وأنا خمس وأربعون ولم تقم لواحد منها بينة، وهذا كله إذا لم يسبق منهما إقرار بالاستيفاء، أما إذا سبق منهما إقرار بالاستيفاء لم تسمع إلا من حيث دعوى الغصب وهي التي لا توجب التحالف اهـ . قال رحمه الله : (وإن قال استوفيت وأخذت بعضه كان القول قول الخصم مع (اليمين لأن يدعي عليه الغصب وهو ينكر والقول قول المنكر قال : ولو اقتسما مائة شاة وقبضا ثم ادعى أحدهما على صاحبه أنك أخذت خمسة من نصيبي غلطاً وأنكر الآخر وقال اقتسمنا على أن يكون لي خمسة وخمسون ولك خمسة وأربعون فالقول قوله مع يمينه لأن القسمة قد تمت ثم ادعى أحدهما على الآخر أنه أخذ خمسة غلطاً وأنكر الآخر؛ فإن قامت بيئة عمل بها وإلا استحلف المدعى عليه؛ كذا الباقي، فأما دعوى يوجب التحالف ؛ فالذي يوجب التحالف أن لا التحالف، ونوع
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And if one of them claims [something] regarding the guarantee of receipt, he is not believed except with evidence. And if he says 'I received and took some of it,' the word is the opponent's word. That one of them has something from his share in the hand of his partner and he admitted receipt, he is not believed except with evidence) because division is a binding contract, and the claimant of error claims the right to rescind for himself after its completion, so it is not accepted except with proof. And if he does not produce evidence, the partners are sworn (against him) because if they admitted that, but when he denies, they are sworn upon him. And someone could say that this proof would require that the person in whose favor the admission was made be sworn if the admitting person claims he lied in his admission, although he is not sworn according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The answer is that this is when the one in whose favor the admission was made admits that the admitting person lied in his admission. But if he does not admit that he lied, it is binding on him, and it does not appear that if he denies, he would be sworn, as they said in our case, not that when he denies he is believed. So they differ, if he swore, there is no way against him, and if he refuses the oath, his share is combined with the share of the other claimant and divided according to their respective rights. They said: It is appropriate that his claim should not be accepted at all because it is contradictory, and this is indicated later where he conditioned mutual oath (tahaluf) if he does not testify against himself regarding receipt. This indicates that if he testified against himself about that, they would not take mutual oath because his claim is not valid due to contradiction. So if mutual oath is prevented due to the invalidity of the claim due to contradiction, then similarly here. Sadr al-Shari'ah said in Sharh al-Wiqayah after quoting what the author of al-Hidayah quoted: 'It is appropriate...' to the end. And in al-Mabsut and Qadi Khan, there is support for this. He said: As for what does not necessitate mutual oath, and the word is the defendant's with his oath, it is when each of them admits receipt, then one of them claims against the other that he wrongfully took something from his share, etc., up to what we mentioned first. He said: Similarly for measurable, weighable, and spatial items, except that for measurable and weighable, when error is proven by evidence, the division is not redone, but the remainder is divided according to their rights because there is no harm in division. For non-uniform items, the division is redone and the remainder is not divided. In al-Tajrid and al-Asl: Error in the amount of what is due by division is of two types: one type necessitates... He claims in the division in a way that does not make him a claimant of usurpation by claiming error, like a hundred sheep between two men who divided them, then one said to his companion: 'Your share is fifty-five (error) and mine is forty-five,' and no one produced evidence. All this is if no admission of receipt preceded from them. If admission of receipt preceded from them, the claim is not heard except as a claim of usurpation, which does not necessitate mutual oath. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And if he says 'I received and took some of it,' the word is the opponent's word with) oath because he claims usurpation against him and he denies, and the word is the denier's. He said: And if they divided a hundred sheep and took possession, then one claimed against his companion: 'You took five from my share by mistake,' and the other denied and said: 'We divided on the basis that I get fifty-five and you get forty-five,' then his word is with his oath because the division is completed. Then if one claimed against the other that he took five by mistake and the other denied, if evidence is produced, it is acted upon; otherwise, the defendant is sworn. Likewise for the remainder. As for the claim that necessitates mutual oath, that which necessitates mutual oath is that [there is] no mutual oath, and a type...
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on claims made after division is complete. The matn states two scenarios: (1) if one partner claims that some of his share is in his partner's hand and the latter admits receipt, the claimant is not believed without evidence; (2) if a partner says 'I received and took some of it' (i.e., admits partial receipt but claims the rest), the opponent's word is taken with oath. The reasoning is that division is a binding contract (عقد لازم), so a claim of error after completion is effectively a claim to rescind, which requires strong proof. If no evidence, the partner who denies is sworn. The commentary then addresses an objection: if the logic required the one in whose favor an admission is made to be sworn when the admitter claims lying, but Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad do not require that oath. The resolution is that if the beneficiary also admits the lie, then there is an issue; otherwise, the admission stands. The text then discusses where mutual oath (تحالف) occurs: when each admits receipt but one claims the other took extra, the defendant's word with oath is taken, and no mutual oath. For fungible items (mikyal, mawzun) if error is proven, the division is not redone but the remainder is redivided; for non-fungibles, the division is redone. The passage ends with a classification of error claims: those that automatically imply usurpation and those that don't, affecting whether mutual oath applies. The student should understand the binding nature of completed division and the strict rules for post-division claims.

Key Terms
تحالف (taḥāluf): Mutual oath between parties when both make claims and there is no evidence; each takes an oath and the property is divided accordingly.
غلط (ghalaṭ): An error in the division, such as one party receiving more than their rightful share due to miscalculation.
الفاسخ (al-fāsikh): The right to rescind a contract; here, the claimant of error is effectively seeking rescission of the division.
إقرار (iqrār): Admission; in this context, a partner's admission of receipt can affect the validity of a subsequent claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute after division of property, what is the Hanafi rule when a partner claims error but produces no evidence?
A) The division is automatically redone.
B) The defendant's word with oath is taken.
C) Both partners are sworn (tahaluf).
D) The claimant's word with oath is taken.

Key Takeaway
A claim of error after a completed division is not acceptable without proof; the defendant's word with oath is authoritative unless evidence is produced.

Claim of Error After Admitting Receipt in Partition
Ruling on a partner who claims error after admitting receipt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a partner claims an error in partition after admitting receipt, and explain why the claim is not accepted without evidence.

Core Idea
Admitting receipt of your share blocks any later claim of error — you cannot contradict your own admission.

This passage from the chapter on Partition (Kitab al-Qismah) addresses a common scenario: after dividing property, one partner claims there was a mistake. But if he already admitted to taking his share, his claim faces a high bar. The Hanafi school treats this as a contradiction, requiring strong evidence. We will explore the reasoning and the procedural steps that follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual context
Note that the claimant has admitted to having received his share (al-istifa') but now claims an error in the partition. This admission is key because it contradicts the later claim.
The admission is a statement against his own interest, but the claim of error seeks to undo the contract.
2
Understand the binding nature of partition
Partition (qismah) is a binding contract (min al-'uqūd al-lāzimah). Once concluded, a party cannot rescind it without proof. The claimant is effectively asking for rescission.
This is analogous to a sale; after delivery and acceptance, claims are restricted.
3
Apply the evidentiary rule
Because the claimant contradicts his own prior admission, he is not believed without evidence (lā yusaddaq illā bi-bayyinah). If he has no evidence, the defendant (the other partner) is sworn (istaḥlaf al-shurakā') to deny the error.
The oath negates the claim; if the defendant refuses, the shares combine and are redistributed.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi refinement
An objector argues that this logic would require swearing the person in whose favor an admission is made if the admitter later claims he lied—but Abu Hanifa and Muhammad do not require that. The answer distinguishes: in our case the claimant's admission creates a contradiction; in the admission-of-lying case, the person favored did not admit to the lie, so the analogy fails.
This shows the school's careful avoidance of contradictory positions.
5
Distinguish from mutual oaths (tahāluf)
The text later clarifies: if no admission of receipt occurred, and the parties disagree on the amount, they take mutual oaths and the division is rescinded. But if admission exists, the claim is treated as one of usurpation (ghasb) rather than error, and mutual oaths are not needed.
Also, for measured/weighed goods, proven error does not redo the division; for heterogeneous goods, it is redone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالاستيفاء لا يصدق إلا ببينة لأن القسمة من العقود اللازمة والمدعي للغلط يدعي حق الفسخ لنفسه بعد تمامها فلا يقبل إلا بحجة، وإن لم يقم ببينة استحلف الشركاء لأنهم لو أقروا بذلك فإذا أنكر وأحلفوا عليه. ولقائل أن هذا الدليل لوجب تحليف المقر له إذا ادعى المقر أنه كذب في إقراره مع أنه لا يحلف عند الإمام ومحمد الجواب أن يقال : إن هذا إذا أقر المقر له أن المقر كذب في إقراره فلو لم يقر المقر له أنه كذب في إقراره لزمه ذلك ولا يظهر فيه أنه لو أنكر استحلف كما لو قالوا فيما نحن فيه لا أنه إذا أنكر كان مصدقاً . في إقراره فافترقا، حلف لم يكن عليه سبيل، ومن نكل عن اليمين جمع نصيبه مع نصيب الآخر المدعي فيقسم على قدر حقوقهما فيه. قالوا: وينبغي أن لا يقبل دعواه أصلاً لأنه متناقض وإليه أشار من بعد حيث شرط التحالف إن لم يشهد على نفسه بالاستيفاء، ويشير بذلك إلى أنه لو شهد على نفسه بذلك لا يتحالفان لأن دعواه لم تصح للتناقض، فإذا منع التحالف لعدم صحة الدعوى للتناقض فكذا هنا. قال صدر الشريعة في شرح الوقاية بعد نقل ما نقل صاحب الهداية : وينبغي إلى آخره. وفي المبسوط وقاضيخان ما يؤيد هذا ا هـ . قال : وأما ما لا يوجب التحالف ويكون القول قول المدعى عليه مع يمينه وهو ما إذا أقر كل واحد منهما بالاستيفاء ثم ادعى أحدهما على الآخر أنه غصب شيئاً من نصيبه إلى آخر ما ذكرناه أولاً قال : وهكذا المكيل والموزون والمذروعات إلا أن يكون في المكيل والموزون متى ثبت الغلط بالبينة لا تعاد القسمة بل يقسم الباقي على قدر حقهم لأنه لا ضرر في قسمة في الأشياء المتفاوتة تعاد للقسمة ولا يقسم الباقي وفي التجريد والأصل: الغلط في مقدار الواجب بالقسمة وهو نوعان: نوع يوجب أحدهما غلظاً يدعي في القسمة على وجه لا يكون مدعياً للغصب بدعوى الغلط كمائة شاة بين رجلين اقتسماها ثم قال أحدهما لصاحبه صابك خمس وخمسون غلظ وأنا خمس وأربعون ولم تقم لواحد منها بينة، وهذا كله إذا لم يسبق منهما إقرار بالاستيفاء، أما إذا سبق منهما إقرار بالاستيفاء لم تسمع إلا من حيث دعوى الغصب وهي التي لا توجب التحالف اهـ .
With regard to al-istifa' (receipt of share), he is not believed except with evidence because the division is one of the binding contracts, and the claimant of error claims the right of rescission for himself after its completion, so he is not accepted except with a proof. And if he does not produce evidence, the partners are sworn because they, if they admitted that, then he denies and they are sworn against him. And it may be said: this proof would necessitate that the person in whose favor the admission is made be sworn when the one who made the admission claims that he lied in his admission, whereas he is not sworn according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] and Muhammad. The answer is that this is when the person in whose favor the admission is made admits that the one who made the admission lied in his admission; if he does not admit that he lied in his admission, that is incumbent upon him, and it is not apparent that if he denies, he is sworn, as they say in our case, not that when he denies he is believed. In his admission, they become distinct; if he swears, there is no way against him, and if he refuses the oath, his share is combined with the share of the other claimant and is divided according to the rights of both in it. They said: it is appropriate that his claim should not be accepted at all because it is contradictory, and to that the author pointed later where he conditioned mutual oaths only if he does not testify against himself regarding receipt, indicating that if he testifies against himself regarding that, they do not take mutual oaths because his claim is invalid due to contradiction. So if mutual oaths are prevented due to the invalidity of the claim for contradiction, then similarly here. Sadr al-Shari'ah said in Sharh al-Wiqayah after quoting what the author of al-Hidayah quoted: 'and it is appropriate...' etc. And in al-Mabsut and Qadikhan there is support for this. He said: As for what does not necessitate mutual oaths and the word is the word of the defendant with his oath, it is when each of them admits receipt, then one of them claims against the other that he wrongfully took something from his share, up to what we mentioned first. He said: And similarly for measured, weighed, and length-measured items, except that for measured and weighed items, when error is established by evidence, the division is not re-done; rather, the remainder is divided according to their rights because there is no harm in division. For heterogeneous items, the division is re-done and the remainder is not divided. And in al-Tajrid and al-Asl: error in the amount of the obligatory [share] in partition is of two types: a type that necessitates a defect that one claims in the partition in a way that he is not a claimant of usurpation through a claim of error, like a hundred sheep between two men: they divided them, then one said to his companion, 'your portion was fifty-five error and mine forty-five,' and neither produced evidence. All this is when no prior admission of receipt has occurred; but if prior admission of receipt has occurred, it is not heard except as a claim of usurpation, and that is the one that does not necessitate mutual oaths.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the book of Partition (Kitab al-Qismah) in the Hanafi school, discussing what happens when a partner claims an error in the partition after having admitted that he took his share (al-istifa'). The author clarifies that such a claim is not accepted without evidence because the partition is a binding contract; the claimant is effectively seeking to rescind the contract, so he must prove his case. If he lacks evidence, the other partners are asked to take an oath denying the error. The text then delves into a nuanced discussion: an objector raises that if this logic were applied consistently, the person in whose favor an admission is made would have to be sworn when the admitter says he lied, but Abu Hanifa and Muhammad do not require that. The answer distinguishes between the two cases: here the claimant's position is contradictory, while in the admission case it is not. The passage also cites later authorities like Sadr al-Shari'ah and Qadikhan to support the ruling that a contradictory claim should be rejected outright. Finally, it outlines two categories of error claims: those that require mutual oaths (when there is no prior admission of receipt) and those that do not (when both parties admit receipt and one claims usurpation). For measured and weighed goods, if error is proven, the division is not redone but the remainder is divided; for heterogeneous goods, the division is redone.

Key Terms
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Receipt of one's share in a partition; admitting to having taken what was allotted.
الغلط (al-ghalat): An error in the partition, such as a miscalculation or unequal distribution.
التحالف (al-tahāluf): Mutual oaths taken by both parties when they disagree and neither has evidence; leads to rescission of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a partition where one party admits to having received his share (استوفيت) and later claims an error, what is the ruling if he has no evidence?
A) The defendant must take an oath.
B) The claimant's word is accepted without evidence.
C) The division is automatically rescinded.
D) Both parties must take mutual oaths.

Key Takeaway
A claim of error in partition after admitting receipt is not heard without evidence; the defendant's oath settles the matter.

Claim of Extra Taking After Partition: The Defendant's Word with Oath
Ruling on a partner's claim of extra taking after partition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a partner claims the other took extra from his share after partition, and explain the basis for accepting the defendant's word with oath.

Core Idea
After a valid partition, a claim of extra taking is ghasb; the denier's word with oath prevails unless evidence is produced.

In disputes over property after a division, subtle distinctions determine who bears the burden of proof. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies how the Hanafi school handles a situation where a partner admits to receiving his share but then alleges the other took some of his portion by mistake. Understanding this ruling illuminates the interplay between the finality of partition and the principle that the denier's word is accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios in the passage
First, a general claim: a person says 'I took my share and also took some of the other's.' Second, a concrete example: partners divide 100 sheep, then one claims the other took five by mistake.
Both involve claims after completion of the partition.
2
Extract the ruling for each
Ruling: In both, the defendant's word with oath is accepted. The claimant must produce evidence; without it, the defendant is sworn.
The ruling is procedural: who has the burden of proof.
3
Understand the rationale (talil)
The author explains: the claimant alleges usurpation (ghasb), and the defendant denies. The Hanafi maxim 'al-qawlu qawlu al-munkir' (the word is the word of the denier) applies.
This maxim shifts the burden to the claimant because the defendant is the one denying the alleged wrong.
4
Note the condition: partition must be complete
The example states 'اقتسما وقبضا' (they divided and took possession). The ruling applies only after the partition is final and possession has transferred.
If the partition itself is in dispute, different rules apply.
5
Recognize the evidentiary rule
If the claimant brings evidence (baiyina), it is acted upon. If not, the defendant is sworn and the claim is dismissed.
This preserves the finality of the completed partition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن قال استوفيت وأخذت بعضه كان القول قول الخصم مع اليمين لأن يدعي عليه الغصب وهو ينكر والقول قول المنكر قال : ولو اقتسما مائة شاة وقبضا ثم ادعى أحدهما على صاحبه أنك أخذت خمسة من نصيبي غلطاً وأنكر الآخر وقال اقتسمنا على أن يكون لي خمسة وخمسون ولك خمسة وأربعون فالقول قوله مع يمينه لأن القسمة قد تمت ثم ادعى أحدهما على الآخر أنه أخذ خمسة غلطاً وأنكر الآخر؛ فإن قامت بيئة عمل بها وإلا استحلف المدعى عليه؛ كذا مع اليمين
He (the author), may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And if he says, 'I have taken (my share) and taken some of it,' the word is the word of the opponent with his oath, because he claims usurpation against him, and he denies, and the word is the word of the denier. He said: And if they divided a hundred sheep and took possession, then one of them claimed against his companion, 'You took five from my share by mistake,' and the other denied and said, 'We divided such that I have fifty-five and you have forty-five,' the word is his word with his oath, because the division has been completed. Then one of them claimed against the other that he took five by mistake, and the other denied; if he produces evidence, it is acted upon, otherwise the defendant is sworn; thus with the oath.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage presents a specific case within the book of Partition. A partner says: 'I took my share and also took some of the other's share' (إستوفيت وأخذت بعضه). This is a claim of both receipt and a subsequent taking, which the author treats as a claim of usurpation (ghasb). Here, the defendant's word is accepted with an oath because he is the denier of the alleged usurpation. The text then illustrates with an example: two partners divide 100 sheep, each takes his share, then one claims the other took five sheep from his portion by mistake. The other denies and claims the division was 55 for him and 45 for the claimant. The defendant's statement is taken with his oath because the division is complete; the claimant must prove his case with evidence. If he has no evidence, the defendant is sworn. This ruling is consistent with the general Hanafi principle that the denier's word is taken when he denies a claim of wrongfully taking.

Key Terms
الغصب (al-ghasb): Wrongful taking of another's property; here, the claimant alleges the defendant took extra from his share.
المنكر (al-munkir): The one who denies the claim; his word is taken with oath in the absence of evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, why is the defendant's word accepted with oath?
A) Because the division is complete
B) Because the claimant is a usurper
C) Because the defendant is the denier of a claimed usurpation
D) Because the claimant already took his share

Key Takeaway
After a valid partition, a claim of extra taking is treated as a new allegation of ghasb; the defendant's statement with oath is accepted unless the claimant produces evidence.

Mutual Oaths in Partition When No Admission of Receipt
Ruling on a partner who claims his lot was not delivered and the other denies, leading to mutual oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mutual oaths in partition disputes and explain its analogue to sale and its limits.

Core Idea
When a partner denies receipt of his lot, mutual oaths rescind the partition, extending sale rules by analogy despite being contrary to qiyas.

Partition disputes can be tricky when one party claims he never received his share and the other denies. Hanafi fiqh provides a specific procedural ruling: mutual oaths (tahāluf) and rescission of the partition. This rule is not automatically analogous to sale, but is justified by the need to resolve the stalemate fairly. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its basis, and its exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Dispute Scenario
You must first identify the key elements: the claimant does not admit having received his share (istifā'), and he asserts that the other's portion is actually his. The other partner denies this claim. Neither has admitted receipt, and there is a dispute over the entitlement itself.
This scenario is different from a claim of defective delivery or an error after receipt.
2
State the Ruling
The text gives the ruling: they take mutual oaths (yatahālifān) and the partition is rescinded (tufsakh al-qisma). The judge does not decide on the basis of default to the defendant because both are claimants in a sense.
Mutual oaths mean each party swears an oath denying the other's claim.
3
Analyze the Analogy to Sale
The author draws an analogy to sale disputes where mutual oaths are established by text (nass) even after possession, contrary to analogy. Here, the dispute centers on what each obtains through the partition, making it similar to a sale disagreement about price and goods.
The text acknowledges the analogy is imperfect: partition combines acknowledgment and exchange.
4
Note the Limits of the Analogy
The passage warns that what is established contrary to analogy cannot be extended by pure qiyas. However, Hanafi scholars apply mutual oaths to partition by considering the essential similarity in the dispute's nature.
This is a point of ikhtilaf: some schools restrict mutual oaths to sale.
5
Apply the Rule with Evidence Present
The ruling is modified if a party produces evidence (bayyinah). In that case, the evidence is acted upon, and the more probative evidence prevails. The mutual oath procedure is only for the absence of evidence.
The text cites Al-Muhit for this exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يقر بالاستيفاء وادعى أن ذا حظه ولم يسلم إليه وكذبه شريكه تحالفاً وفسخت القسمة لأن الاختلاف فيما يحصل له بالقسمة فصار نظير الاختلاف في البيع والثمن ا هـ . ولا يخفى أنه يبدأ بيمين أيهما شاء ولقائل أن يقول : التحالف في البيع فيما إذا كان قبل القبض على وفاق القياس كما علم في محله، وأما بعد القبض فمخالف للقياس لأن أحدهما لا يدعي على الآخر شيئاً حتى ينكره الآخر فيحلف عليه والآخر يدعي ولكنا عرفناه في البيع بالنص، وفيما تحن فيه بالتحالف مخالف للقياس لأن كلاً منهما ليس مدعياً وهو وارد في البيع بعد القبض على خلاف القياس، وقد تقرر أن ما ورد على خلاف القياس فغيره عليه لا يقاس ولا يمكن إلحاقه بطريق دلالة النص لأن القسمة ليست في معنى البيع من وجه إذ فيها معنى الإقرار والمبادلة معاً فليتأمل في الجواب قال : فإن أراد أحدهما القسمة بعد التحالف فليس له ذلك لأنه لا يمكن لأنها لا تكون إلا بالقرعة وقد يقع نصيب أحدهما في جانب الآخر فيتضرر . وقال في موضع آخر : ولو أقام أحدهما بينة عمل بها، ولو أقام بينة عمل بالبينة التي هي أكثر إثباتاً ؛ كذا في المحيط . وقيد أيضاً قسم القسام الدار فأعطى أحدهم أكثر حقه غلطاً من وبنى فيها فإنهم يستقبلون القسمة فإن وقع البناء في قسم غيره دفع نقصه ولا يرجع على القاسم بقيمة البناء ويرجعون عليه بالآجر الذي أخذه، وإذا قسما دوراً وأخذ أحدهما داراً والآخر أخرى ثم ادعى أحدهما غلطاً وجاء بالبينة فإنه ينقص القسمة ا هـ .
And if he does not admit receipt and claims that this is his lot and it was not delivered to him, and his partner denies him, they take mutual oaths and the partition is rescinded, because the disagreement is about what he obtains through the partition, so it becomes analogous to disagreement in sale regarding price and goods. And it is not hidden that one begins with the oath of whichever he wishes. And it may be said: mutual oaths in sale occur before possession according to analogy, as is known in its place; after possession it is contrary to analogy because neither of them claims anything from the other such that the other denies and is sworn, and the other is the claimant. But we know it in sale by text (nass), and in our case mutual oaths are contrary to analogy because each of them is not a claimant, and it occurs in sale after possession contrary to analogy. And it has been established that what occurs contrary to analogy cannot be analogized to other cases, nor can it be attached by way of textual indication because partition is not in the meaning of sale in one respect, for it contains the meaning of acknowledgment and exchange together. So let one reflect on the answer. He said: If one of them wants partition after mutual oaths, he does not have that because it is not possible, as it can only be by lottery, and the share of one may fall in the area of the other, causing harm. And he said in another place: If one of them presents evidence, it is acted upon; if he presents evidence, the evidence that is more probative is acted upon; thus in al-Muhit. And it is also conditioned: the arbitrator divided the house and gave one more than his right by mistake, and he built in it; then they restart the division; if the building occurs in the share of another, he compensates for the deficiency and does not claim from the divider the value of the building, and they claim from him the bricks he took. And if they divided houses and one took one house and the other another, then one claimed error and brought evidence, the division is annulled.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a partner does NOT admit to having taken his share (استيفاء), but instead claims that the other's portion actually belongs to him and was not handed over. The other denies. Here, since neither side has admitted receipt and the dispute is about what each should receive, the ruling is that they take mutual oaths (تحالف) and the partition is rescinded. This is analogous to a sale dispute after possession but before payment, which also requires mutual oaths per textual evidence (nass), though it is contrary to analogy. The author notes that the analogy to sale is not perfect because partition involves elements of both acknowledgment and exchange. After mutual oaths, neither party can demand a new partition immediately because it would cause harm. If one party has evidence, it is accepted; the more probative evidence is preferred. The text also includes a related case: if a court-appointed divider mistakenly gives one partner more than his share and the partner builds on the property, the partition is redone, and the partner who built must compensate if his building ends up on another's share.

Key Terms
التحالف (al-tahāluf): Mutual oaths taken by both parties when they disagree and neither has evidence; leads to rescission of the contract.
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Receipt of one's share; here, the claimant does not admit to having taken his share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when a partner claims his lot was not delivered and the other denies, without any prior admission of receipt?
A) The claimant must bring evidence or lose.
B) The defendant's word is taken with oath.
C) They take mutual oaths and the partition is rescinded.
D) The partition stands and the claimant can only claim usurpation.

Key Takeaway
When a partner does not admit receipt and the other denies, mutual oaths are taken and the partition is rescinded; this rule is extended from sale despite being contrary to analogy.

Gross Fraud (Ghabn Fahish) in Partition: Rescission and Evidence Rules
Ruling on gross fraud rescinding partition and summary of types of error claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gross fraud in partition and apply the procedural rules for evidence and oaths when a party claims error.

Core Idea
A partition is rescinded if gross fraud appears — even if by mutual consent — because the agreement is tainted by deception.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq clarifies when a partition can be undone due to gross fraud. The author distinguishes between partitions by a judge and by mutual consent, and resolves an intra-Hanafi disagreement. Additionally, he outlines the rules of evidence and mutual oaths when one party claims a specific part was wrongly assigned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on gross fraud in partition
State that gross fraud (ghabn fahish) causes rescission. Note the two scenarios: partition by a judge (clearly rescinded) and by mutual consent (controversial, but the relied-upon view rescinds).
The ruling is procedural: the partition is undone.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Some scholars analogized to sale: a claim of fraud is not considered after mutual consent. But the correct view rescinds anyway because gross fraud vitiates consent itself.
The text cites al-Kafi and al-Inayah for the sound view.
3
Understand the evidence rules for disputed shares
If one party claims a room is his and the other denies, the claimant must bring evidence. If both bring evidence, the claimant's is preferred because he is the external party (al-kharij). If no evidence, they take mutual oaths and the partition is rescinded.
The principle 'بينة الخارج مقدمة' (evidence of external claimant is preferred) governs.
4
Trace the process for boundary disputes
If they differ on boundaries and both have evidence, each is given the part in the other's hand (since each is external regarding that part). If only one has evidence, it is accepted.
This applies the same external-claimant rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولو ظهر غبن فاحش في القسمة (تفسخ وهذا إذا كانت بقضاء القاضي فظاهر لأن تصر رفه مقيد بالعدل والنظر، وأما إذا كان بالتراضي فقد قيل لا يلتفت إلى قول دعوى الغبن لا تعتبر في البيع فكذا في القسمة لوجود . د التراضي وفيه يفسخ هو لان الصحيح؛ ذكره في الكافي وفي العناية : وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى. وإذا اقتسما داراً وأصاب كل واحد منهما جانباً وادعى أحدهما بيتاً في يد الآخر أنه مما أصابه بالقسمة وأنكر الآخر فعليه إقامة البينة، وإن أقاما البينة فبينة المدعي مقدمة لأنه الخارج، وإن كان قبل الإشهاد تحالفا وتفسخ، ولو اختلفا في الحدود وأقاما البينة يقضى لكل واحد منهما بالجزء الذي في يد صاحبه لأنه خارج فيه وبينة الخارج مقدمة وإن أقاما أحدهما بينة يقضى بها وإن دعوى القسمة الغلط لم يقم لواحد منهما بينة تحالفا وترادا كما في البيع . قال : في القسمة نوعان : ما يصح وما لا يصح. وما يصح نوعان: ما يوجب التحالف وما لا يوجب التحالف . أما ما لا يدعي أحدهم الغلط في التقويم بغبن يسير وهو ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم
He (the author), may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And if gross fraud appears in the partition, it is rescinded. This is if it was by the judgment of a judge, because his disposal is restricted by justice and consideration. As for if it was by mutual consent, it has been said that no attention is paid to the claim of fraud; a claim of fraud is not considered in sale, so similarly in partition, because mutual consent exists. And there is a view that it is rescinded anyway, and the sound view is the latter; it is mentioned in al-Kafi and in al-Inayah: it is the correct view and upon it is the fatwa. And if they divided a house and each got a side, and one claimed a room in the other's hand that it was part of his share in the division, and the other denied, he must produce evidence. If both produce evidence, the evidence of the claimant is given precedence because he is the external party (al-kharij). If it was before testifying, they take mutual oaths and it is rescinded. And if they differed about boundaries and both produced evidence, judgment is given to each for the part that is in the hand of the other, because he is external regarding it, and the evidence of the external is given precedence. And if one of them produces evidence, it is judged accordingly. And if a claim of error in partition is made and neither produces evidence, they take mutual oaths and return (the property) as in sale. He said: In partition, there are two types: what is valid and what is invalid. And what is valid is of two types: what necessitates mutual oaths and what does not necessitate mutual oaths. As for what does not necessitate mutual oaths, it is when neither claims error in valuation due to minor fraud, which does not fall under valuation.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This final passage covers two topics: (1) Gross fraud (ghabn fahish) in a partition: if the partition was carried out by a judge, it is rescinded because the judge must act justly. If it was by mutual consent, there is a difference of opinion: some say the claim of fraud is not considered because both parties agreed, while the correct view (as in al-Kafi and al-Inayah) is that it is rescinded anyway; this is the fatwa position. (2) The passage then discusses disputes over specific parts after a house partition: if one claims a room is his and the other denies, the claimant must bring evidence; if both have evidence, the claimant's is preferred because he is the one asserting a right (al-kharij). If the dispute precedes any testimony (i.e., before they have made formal claims), they take mutual oaths and the partition is rescinded. If they differ on boundaries and both have evidence, each is given the part in the other's hand because they are external to that part. Finally, the author summarizes that partition claims are of two types: valid and invalid. Valid partitions are further divided into those requiring mutual oaths (when error is claimed without admission of receipt) and those not (when minor fraud is claimed that does not affect the evaluation). The text cuts off here, but the meaning is clear.

Key Terms
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghabn al-fāḥish): A gross disparity in value or share that indicates fraud or error; it causes rescission of the partition.
الخارج (al-khārij): The party whose claim is external to the current possession; his evidence is preferred because he is the one asserting a right over property in another's hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The claim of fraud is ignored and the partition stands.
B) The partition is rescinded despite the mutual consent.
C) The parties must first take mutual oaths before any rescission.
D) Only the judge who originally oversaw the partition can rescind it.

Key Takeaway
Gross fraud (ghabn fahish) voids a partition even if made by mutual consent, and in disputes over specific shares, the evidence of the external claimant is preferred.

Mutual Oaths and Annulment When One Denies Delivery of Share
Explaining the ruling of mutual oaths and annulment when a partner denies delivery of the share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that mutual oaths (tahaluf) lead to annulment of a partition when one partner denies delivery, and explain the qiyas argument that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
Mutual oaths in partition are applied by analogy to sale, despite being contrary to strict qiyas.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Ibn Nujaym explains a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: when a partner denies receiving his share and the other denies the claim, they take mutual oaths and the partition is annulled. The ruling is based on analogy to disputes in sale, but the commentator notes a subtle objection — the analogy is weak because partition combines elements of acknowledgment and exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
What exactly triggers this ruling? The text says: a partner does not admit having received his share (lam yuqirr bil-istifa) and claims the other partner took his luck and did not deliver it to him, and the other partner denies this claim.
Focus on the three conditions: denial of receipt, claim of non-delivery, and denial by the other.
2
State the legal consequence
The ruling: they take mutual oaths (tahalafa) and the partition is annulled (fusikhat al-qisma). This means the division is voided and the property reverts to co-ownership.
The annulment is a direct result of the mutual oaths, not merely a single oath.
3
Analyze the dalil: qiyas on sale
The commentator justifies the ruling by analogy to sale: because the dispute is about what each obtained through partition, it resembles a dispute over price in a sale. In both cases, mutual oaths are prescribed.
The illa (effective cause) is the existence of a dispute over entitlement.
4
Consider the objection (qiyas contrary to original)
Someone objects that in sale, mutual oaths are only according to qiyas before possession; after possession they are contrary to qiyas and known by text. In partition, neither party is a pure claimant (mudda'i) or defendant, so the analogy is even weaker.
This objection raises an important methodological issue: can an exception be extended by analogy?
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The commentator does not reject the objection but advises reflection (falyata'ammal). He hints that partition is unique because it combines elements of acknowledgment (iqrar) and exchange (mubadala), so the ruling stands on its own basis, perhaps through custom or istihsan.
The Hanafi school upholds the ruling despite the weak qiyas, showing practical legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع اليمين وإن لم يقر بالاستيفاء وادعى أن ذا حظه ولم يسلم إليه وكذبه شريكه تحالفاً وفسخت القسمة قال رحمه الله : (وإن لم يقر بالاستيفاء وادعى أن ذا حظه ولم يسلم إليه وكذبه شريكه تحالفاً وفسخت القسمة) لأن الاختلاف فيما يحصل له بالقسمة فصار نظير الاختلاف في البيع والثمن ا هـ . ولا يخفى أنه يبدأ بيمين أيهما شاء ولقائل أن يقول : التحالف في البيع فيما إذا كان قبل القبض على وفاق القياس كما علم في محله، وأما بعد القبض فمخالف للقياس لأن أحدهما لا يدعي على الآخر شيئاً حتى ينكره الآخر فيحلف عليه والآخر يدعي ولكنا عرفناه في البيع بالنص، وفيما نحن فيه بالتحالف مخالف للقياس لأن كلاً منهما ليس مدعياً وهو وارد في البيع بعد القبض على خلاف القياس، وقد تقرر أن ما ورد على خلاف القياس فغيره عليه لا يقاس ولا يمكن إلحاقه بطريق دلالة النص لأن القسمة ليست في معنى البيع من وجه إذ فيها معنى الإقرار والمبادلة معاً فليتأمل في الجواب
With the oath: If he does not admit taking and claims that that is his luck and it was not delivered to him, and his partner denies him, they both take oaths and the partition is annulled. The author said: (If he does not admit taking and claims that that is his luck and it was not delivered to him, and his partner denies him, they both take oaths and the partition is annulled) because the dispute is about what he obtained through partition, so it becomes analogous to dispute in sale and price. It is not hidden that one begins with the oath of whichever he wishes. Someone may say: Mutual oaths in sale are before possession according to analogy, as known in its place; after possession it is contrary to analogy because one does not claim anything from the other so that the other denies and takes an oath, and the other claims. But we know it in sale by text, and in our case mutual oaths are contrary to analogy because neither is a claimant, and it is reported in sale after possession contrary to analogy. It has been established that what is reported contrary to analogy, other than it, is not measured by it, nor can it be attached by way of textual indication because partition is not equivalent to sale in one respect, for it contains both the sense of acknowledgment and exchange. So let one reflect on the answer.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states: If a partner does not admit taking possession of his share and claims that the other partner took his luck and did not deliver it, and the other denies, then they take mutual oaths (tahaluf) and the partition is annulled. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) explains that the basis for this ruling is analogy to sale: when there is a dispute about the price in a sale, mutual oaths are required. Here the dispute is about what each obtained in the partition, so it is analogous. However, he notes an objection: in sale, mutual oaths are according to analogy only before possession; after possession, they are contrary to analogy but established by text. In partition, both parties are not truly claimants (mudda'i) and defendants, so the analogy is even weaker. Yet, the ruling is accepted because partition combines elements of acknowledgment (iqrar) and exchange (mubadala), making it unique. The commentator advises careful reflection, implying the ruling is based on custom and necessity.

Key Terms
تحالف (tahāluf): Mutual oaths taken by both parties when they dispute over the subject of a contract, each swearing to the truth of their claim.
قسمة (qisma): Partition of jointly owned property (musha') into individual shares.
استيفاء (istīfā'): Taking possession or receiving one's share entirely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The partner who claims must provide proof.
B) They take mutual oaths and the partition is annulled.
C) The partition stands, and the judge decides based on evidence.
D) The denying partner must compensate the other.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when one partner denies delivery of his share and the other denies the claim, the dispute is resolved through mutual oaths and annulment of the partition, based on analogy to sale despite being contrary to strict qiyas.

Gross Defect Annuls Partition: Qadi vs Mutual Consent
Ruling on gross defect annulling partition with qadi vs mutual consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gross defect in partition and distinguish between partition by qadi's decree and mutual consent.

Core Idea
A gross defect annuls a qadi-ordered partition, but not a mutually agreed one—consent overrides hidden imbalance.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains when a gross defect (ghubn fahish) invalidates a partition. The key distinction is between partition ordered by a qadi, which is bound by justice, and partition by mutual consent, where the parties' agreement precludes later complaint. The text also discusses evidence rules and the definition of gross vs. slight defect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The matn states gross defect annuls partition. But the condition is that the partition was made by a qadi's decree. The qadi's action is restricted by justice and consideration, so if gross defect appears, the partition is annulled.
The phrase 'اذا كانت بقضاء القاضي' (if by decree of qadi) is the key condition.
2
Contrast with mutual consent partition
If the partition was by mutual consent, the correct Hanafi view (al-sahih) is that the claim of gross defect is not entertained, by analogy to sale where a claim of gross defect after delivery is not accepted. Mutual consent implies acceptance of the shares as they are.
There is a differing opinion (qila) that gross defect annuls even in mutual consent, but the sahih view prevails.
3
Apply the evidence rules for disputes
If one party claims a room in the other's hand is from his share, the claimant must provide evidence. If both provide evidence, the claimant's (the external party's) evidence is preferred. If before witnessing (ishhad), they take mutual oaths and the partition is annulled.
This mirrors evidence rules in sale disputes.
4
Understand the distinction between gross and slight defect
A slight defect (ghubn yasir) is what valuers could reasonably differ on and does not annul. A gross defect (ghubn fahish) is beyond tolerable estimation and annuls partition under the qadi's decree.
The text says: 'ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين' (what is not under the estimation of valuers) defines gross defect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولو ظهر غبن فاحش في القسمة (تفسخ وهذا إذا كانت بقضاء القاضي فظاهر لأن تصر[؟] رفه مقيد بالعدل والنظر، وأما إذا كان بالتراضي فقد قيل لا يلتفت إلى قول دعوى الغبن لا تعتبر في البيع فكذا في القسمة لوجود . د التراضي وفيه يفسخ هو مدعيه [؟] لأن الصحيح؛ ذكره في الكافي وفي العناية : وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى. وإذا اقتسما داراً وأصاب كل واحد منهما جانباً وادعى أحدهما بيتاً في يد الآخر أنه مما أصابه بالقسمة وأنكر الآخر فعليه إقامة البينة، وإن أقاما البينة فبينة المدعي مقدمة لأنه الخارج، وإن كان قبل الإشهاد تحالفا وتفسخ، ولو اختلفا في الحدود وأقاما البينة يقضى لكل واحد منهما بالجزء الذي في يد صاحبه لأنه خارج فيه وبينة الخارج مقدمة وإن أقاما أحدهما بينة يقضى بها وإن دعوى نوعان : ما القسمة الغلط لم يقم لواحد منهما بينة تحالفا وترادا كما في البيع . قال : في يصح وما لا يصح. وما يصح نوعان: ما التحالف وما لا التحالف . أما ما لا يدعي أحدهم الغلط في التقويم بغبن يسير وهو ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم
The author said: (If a gross defect appears in the partition, it is annulled.) This is if it was by the decree of the qadi; it is apparent because his ruling [؟] is restricted by justice and consideration. But if it was by mutual consent, it has been said that no attention is paid to the claim, as the claim of gross defect is not considered in sale, so likewise in partition due to mutual consent. And there it is annulled [؟] because the correct [view] is mentioned in al-Kafi and al-Inaya: it is the correct view and on it is the fatwa. If two partition a house, each getting a side, and one claims a room in the other's hand is from his share and the other denies, then he must provide evidence; if both provide evidence, the evidence of the claimant is preferred because he is the external party; if before witnessing, they take mutual oaths and it is annulled. If they differ about boundaries and both provide evidence, judgment is given for each regarding the part in the other's hand because he is external and the evidence of the external is preferred. If only one provides evidence, judgment is given by it. The claims are of two types: what necessitates annulment and what does not. What requires annulment is when neither provides evidence: they take mutual oaths and reciprocate as in sale. He said: There is what is valid and what is not valid. What is valid is of two types: what requires mutual oaths and what does not. As for what one does not claim error in valuation due to a slight defect, which is what the valuers do not consider [significant].
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on gross defect (ghubn fahish) in partition. The matn states that if a gross defect appears, the partition is annulled. The commentator clarifies that this applies when the partition was made by a qadi's decree, as the qadi's action is bound by justice. If it was by mutual consent, the correct view is that the claim of gross defect is not entertained, comparable to sale where a gross defect claim after delivery is not accepted, because both parties agreed. The text then discusses related scenarios: if one claims a specific room in the other's hand, evidence rules apply; if both have evidence, the claimant's evidence is preferred; if before witnesses (ishhad), they take oaths and annul; for boundary disputes, each gets the part in the other's hand based on external evidence. Finally, it distinguishes between valid and invalid claims: a slight defect (ghubn yasir) does not annul, but a gross defect does. This aligns with the Hanafi position that gross defects in partition are grounds for annulment only if the partition was by a judge, not by mutual consent.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghubn fāḥish): A gross defect or inequality in valuation that is beyond the estimation of competent valuers, making the partition unfair.
غبن يسير (ghubn yasīr): A slight defect or inequality that valuers could reasonably differ on; it does not annul partition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Only if the partition was by mutual consent.
D) Only if both parties take mutual oaths.

Key Takeaway
Gross defect annuls partition only when the partition was ordered by a qadi; mutual consent precludes annulment.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Reclamation of a Common Portion from a Partner's Share
Intra-Hanafi dispute on reclamation of common portion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on whether partition is annulled when a common portion of one partner's share is reclaimed and apply the tarjih ruling to a practical example.

Core Idea
Reclamation of a common portion does not annul partition unless the whole property becomes common again.

After a partition, if a third party proves ownership of a portion of one partner's share, does the partition break? There is a known intra-Hanafi dispute. This lesson presents the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf, and the relied-upon ruling. Understanding this distinction helps in property law and inheritance cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the three-way distinction
The passage first distinguishes three cases: reclamation of a specific part of a share (consensus no annulment), reclamation of a common portion of a share (dispute), reclamation of a common portion of the whole (consensus annulment). Identify which case is in dispute.
The dispute is only about the second case: common portion of one share.
2
State the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They hold that partition remains valid; the affected partner takes proportional compensation from the other partner's share (or may return his remaining share and re-partition). The reasoning: the purpose of partition (distinction and separation) is still achieved.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State the position of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf says partition is annulled because a new partner appears, making the original partition invalid by analogy to reclamation of a common portion of the whole.
This is the second position.
4
Analyze the proofs and response
Both sides use qiyas (analogy). Abu Hanifa analogises to permissible initial partitions with shared portions; Abu Yusuf analogises to reclamation of the whole common portion. The text supports Abu Hanifa and Muhammad as more correct.
The tarjih is explicit: 'والأول أصح' (the first is more correct).
5
Apply the ruling to a numerical example
The passage gives an example: if one share is 600 and the other also 600, and half of one is reclaimed, the affected partner recovers half of half = 150 from the other's share.
This illustrates proportional compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقومين ولا تعاد القسمة به لأنه لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه، والذي يصح فيه الدعوى هو يدعي الغلط بغبن فاحش وهو ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين ؛ كذا في المحيط ا هـ . قال رحمه الله : (ولو) استحق بعض شائع من حظه رجع بقسطه في حظ شريكه ولا تفسخ وهذا عند الإمام، وظاهر عبارة المؤلف أن هذا محتم لكن قال في العناية : إن شاء رجع بذلك إلى نصيب صاحبه، وإن شاء رد ما بقي واقتسما ثانياً عند الإمام. وقوله «بقسطه» يعني لو كان قيمة نصيبه ستمائة وقيمة الآخر مثله فاستحق نصف ما في يده رجع بنصف النصف وهو الربع وهو مائة وخمسون. وقال الثاني : تفسخ كذا ذكر الاختلاف في الجزء الشائع في الأسرار وغيره، قيد بالشائع يحترز عن المعين. وذكر القدوري إذا استحق بعض نصيب بعض أحدهما بعينه فالصحيح أن الاختلاف في الشائع، وفي استحقاق البعض المعين لا تفسخ بالإجماع، ولو استحق بعض شائع في الكل تفسخ بالإجماع فهذه ثلاثة أوجه، ومحمد مع الإمام فيما حكاه أو حفص، ومع الثاني فيما حكاه أبو سليمان والأول أصح. للثاني أن يأخذ بالاستحقاق ظهر شريك آخر والقسمة بدونه لا تصح فصار كما لو استحق بعض الشائع في الكل بخلاف المعين لأن ما وراء المستحق بقي مقرراً على حاله ليس للغير فيه حق. ولهما أن المقصود بالقسمة التميز والإفراز ولا ينعدم باستحقاق جزء شائع من نصيب الواحد ولهذا جازت القسمة في الابتداء على هذا الوجه بأن كان البعض المتقدم مشتركاً بين ثلاثة نفر والبعض المؤخر بين اثنين فاقتسم الاثنان على أن لأحدهما مالهما من المقدم وللآخر المؤخر أو اقتسما على أن لأحدهما مالهما من المقدم وبعض المؤخر مفرزاً يجوز فكذا هذا بخلاف استحقاق الشائع في الكل لأن معنى الإفراز والتميز لم يتحقق مع بقاء نصيب البعض. ولو استحق نصيب أحدهم كله يرجع به على الشركاء، ولو باع بعضهم بفضل نصيبه شائعاً ثم استحق بعض ما بقي شائعاً كان له أن يرجع على الشركاء بحسابه وسقط خيار الفسخ ببيع البعض. وعند أبي يوسف يرجع على ما في أيديهم بحسابه ويضمن حصتهم مما باع لأن القسمة تنقلب فاسدة عنده والمقبوض بالفاسد مملوك وينفذ بيعه وهو مضمون بالقيمة فيضمن لهم، ولو قسم الورثة التركة ثم ظهر فيها دين محيط قيل للورثة اقضوا دين الميت، فإن قضوه صحت القسمة وإلا فسخت لأن الدين مقدم على الإرث فيمتنع وقوع الملك لهم إلا إذا قضوا الدين أو أبرأهم الغرماء فيصح لزوال المانع ، ولو كان الدين مستغرقاً فكذا الجواب إلا إذا بقي من التركة ما يفي بالدين فحينئذ لا تفسخ لعدم الحاجة. ولو ادعى أحد المتقاسمين للتركة ديناً في التركة صح دعواه ولا تناقض لأن الدين يتعلق بالذمة والقسمة تصادف الصورة، ولو ادعى عيباً بأي سبب كأن لم تسمع دعواه لأن الإقدام على الشركة اعتراف بأن المقسوم مشترك قال : ولو كان بينهما مائة شاة أخذ أحدهما أربعين
The valuers, and the partition is not repeated because it cannot be avoided; the valid claim is when one claims error due to a gross defect which is not within the estimation of valuers; so in al-Muhit. The author said: (If) a common portion of his luck is reclaimed, he returns proportionally from his partner's luck and the partition is not annulled. This according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The author's expression appears to be probable, but al-Inaya said: If he wishes, he can take compensation from his partner's share, and if he wishes he can return what remains and they partition a second time, according to Imam. His saying 'proportionally' means if the value of his share is 600 and the other's is like it, and half of what is in his hand is reclaimed, he returns half of the half, which is a quarter, i.e., 150. The second (Abu Yusuf) said: It is annulled. Thus the disagreement is mentioned regarding the common portion in al-Asrar etc. It is restricted by 'common' to exclude specific. Al-Quduri mentioned: If a specific portion of one's share is reclaimed, the correct view is that the disagreement is only about the common; regarding a specific portion, there is no annulment by consensus; and if a common portion of the whole is reclaimed, it is annulled by consensus. So there are three aspects. Muhammad agrees with Imam according to what Hafs narrated, and with the second according to what Abu Sulayman narrated; the first is more correct. For the second: due to reclamation, another partner appears, and the partition without him is not valid, so it becomes as if a common portion of the whole was reclaimed, unlike a specific portion because what remains beyond the reclaimed is fixed as it is, no one else has a right to it. For them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): the purpose of partition is distinction and separation, and it is not nullified by reclamation of a common portion from the share of one, and therefore partition is permissible initially in this manner: if part of the property is shared among three and part among two, and the two partition such that one gets what they have from the former and the other gets the latter, or they partition such that one gets what they have from the former and some of the latter separated, it is permissible. So likewise here, unlike reclamation of a common portion of the whole because the sense of separation and distinction is not achieved with the remaining share of some. If the entire share of one is reclaimed, he returns proportionally to the partners. If one sells part of his share as common, then some of what remains is reclaimed as common, he may return proportionally to the partners, and the option to rescind (khiyar faskh) drops due to the sale. According to Abu Yusuf, he returns proportionally from what is in their hands and guarantees their share from what he sold, because the partition becomes void in his view, and what is taken under a void contract is owned, and his sale is valid and it is guaranteed by value, so he guarantees for them. If the heirs partition the estate and then an encompassing debt appears, the heirs are told to pay the deceased's debt; if they pay, the partition is valid; otherwise it is annulled, because the debt precedes inheritance, so ownership for them is impossible unless they pay the debt or the creditors release them, then it becomes valid due to removal of the impediment. If the debt is encompassing, the same answer applies unless there remains enough from the estate to cover the debt, then it is not annulled due to no need. If one of the partititioners claims a debt against the estate, his claim is valid and not contradictory because the debt relates to the liability while the partition concerns the property. If he claims a defect for any reason, his claim is not heard because proceeding with the partnership is an acknowledgment that what is partitioned is shared. He said: If they have 100 sheep and one takes 40.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of reclamation (istihqaq) of a common portion from one partner's share after partition. The matn states the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: the partner whose share suffers reclamation recovers proportionally from his partner's share, and the partition is not annulled. He may either take compensation or return the remainder and re-partition. The commentator explains the calculation with an example. Abu Yusuf holds that the partition is annulled because the reclamation introduces a third partner, making the original partition invalid without him, analogous to reclamation of a common portion of the whole. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that the purpose of partition—distinction and separation—is still achieved; only a portion of one share is affected, and the rest remains distinct. They support this by showing that such partition is permissible initially in certain cases. The passage also distinguishes three scenarios: (1) reclamation of a specific part of a share—consensus no annulment; (2) reclamation of a common portion of a share—dispute as above; (3) reclamation of a common portion of the whole—consensus annulment. The correct position (al-awla asahh) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The text then covers additional scenarios: full reclamation of one's entire share, sale before reclamation, and debts after partition among heirs. These are related applications of the same principles: partition stands unless it fails to achieve its purpose or is invalidated by overriding claims.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): Reclamation by a third party of a right (ownership) in the partitioned property, proving it belonged to them.
شائع (shā'iʿ): A common or undivided portion; a share that is not physically delineated.
معين (muʿayyan): A specific, physically identified portion of property.
تفسخ (tufsakh): Annulment of the partition; it becomes void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the consequence when a common portion (shayi') of one partner's share is reclaimed by a third party?
A) The partition is annulled, and the property reverts to pre-partition co-ownership.
B) The partition remains valid; the affected partner takes proportional compensation from the other partner's share.
C) The reclaimant becomes a co-owner in the entire property, and the partition is automatically adjusted.
D) The affected partner must return his entire share to the other partner and they re-partition.

Key Takeaway
Reclamation of a common portion from one partner's share does not annul the partition; the affected partner recovers proportionally from the other partner's share.
